\"configured\", cfg.RetryConfig.MaxAttempts, \"actual\", minMaxAttempts)\n   146→\t\tcfg.RetryConfig.MaxAttempts = minMaxAttempts\n   147→\t}\n   148→\n   149→\tsch := schedule{\n   150→\t\tregistry:               newRuleRegistry(),\n   151→\t\tretryConfig:            cfg.RetryConfig,\n   152→\t\tclock:                  cfg.C,\n   153→\t\tbaseInterval:           cfg.BaseInterval,\n   154→\t\tlog: 174→\n   175→func (sch *schedule) Run(ctx context.Context) error {\n   176→\tsch.log.Info(\"Starting scheduler\", \"tickInterval\", sch.baseInterval, \"maxAttempts\", sch.retryConfig.MaxAttempts)\n   177→\tt := ticker.New(sch.clock, sch.baseInterval, sch.metrics.Ticker, sch.log)\n   178→\tdefer t.Stop()\n   179→\n   180→\tif err := sch.schedulePeriodic(ctx, t); err != nil {\n   181→\t\tsch.log.Error(\"Failure while running the rule evaluation loop\", \"error\", err)\n   182→\t}\n   183→\treturn nil\n   184→}\n   185→\n   186→// Rules fetches the entire set of rules considered for evaluation by the scheduler on the next tick.\n   187→// Such rules are not guaranteed to have been evaluated by the scheduler.\n   188→// Rules returns all supplementary metadata for the rules that is stored by the scheduler - namely, the set of folder titles.\n   189→func (sch *schedule) Rules() ([]*ngmodels.AlertRule, map[ngmodels.FolderKey]string) {\n   190→\treturn   201→// deleteAlertRule stops evaluation of the rule, deletes it from active rules, and cleans up state cache.\n   202→func (sch *schedule) deleteAlertRule(ctx context.Context, keys ...ngmodels.AlertRuleKey) {\n   203→\tfor _, key := range keys {\n   204→\t\t// It can happen that the scheduler has deleted the alert rule before the\n   205→\t\t// Ruler API has called DeleteAlertRule. This can happen as requests to\n   206→\t\t// the Ruler API do not hold an exclusive lock over all scheduler operations.\n   207→\t\t_, ok := sch.schedulableAlertRules.del(key)\n   208→\t\tif !ok {\n   209→\t\t\tsch.log.Info(\"Alert rule cannot be removed from the scheduler as it is not scheduled\", key.LogContext()...)\n   210→\t\t}\n   211→\t\t// Delete the rule routine\n   212→\t\truleRoutine, ok := sch.registry.del(key)\n   213→\t\tif !ok {\n   214→\t\t\tsch.log.Info(\"Alert rule cannot be stopped as it is not running\", key.LogContext()...)\n   215→\t\t\tcontinue\n   216→\t\t}\n   217→\n   218→\t\t// stop rule evaluation\n   219→\t\treason := sch.getRuleStopReason(ctx, ruleRoutine.Identifier())\n   220→\t\truleRoutine.Stop(reason)\n   221→\t}\n   222→\t// Our best bet at this point is that we update the metrics with what we hope to schedule in the next tick.\n   223→\talertRules, _ := sch.schedulableAlertRules.all()\n   224→\tsch.updateRulesMetrics(alertRules)\n   225→}\n   226→\n   227→func (sch *schedule) getRuleStopReason(ctx context.Context, key ngmodels.AlertRuleKeyWithGroup) error {\n   228→\t// If the ruleStopReasonProvider is defined, we will use it to get the reason why the\n   229→\t// alert rule was stopped. If it returns an error, we will use the default reason.\n   230→\tif sch.ruleStopReasonProvider == nil {\n   231→\t\treturn errRuleDeleted\n   232→\t}\n   233→\n   234→\tstopReason, err := sch.ruleStopReasonProvider.FindReason(ctx, sch.log, key)\n   235→\tif err != nil {\n   236→\t\tsch.log.New(key.LogContext()...).Error(\"Failed to get stop reason\", \"error\", err)\n   237→\t\treturn errRuleDeleted\n   238→\t}\n   239→\tif stopReason == nil {\n   240→\t\treturn errRuleDeleted\n   241→\t}\n   242→\n   243→\treturn stopReason\n   244→}\n   245→\n   246→func (sch *schedule) schedulePeriodic(ctx context.Context, t *ticker.T) error {\n   247→\tdispatcherGroup, ctx := errgroup.WithContext(ctx)\n   248→\tfor {\n   249→\t\tselect {\n   250→\t\tcase tick := <-t.C:\n   251→\t\t\t// We use Round(0) on the start time to remove the monotonic clock.\n   252→\t\t\t// This is required as ticks from the ticker and time.Now() can have\n   253→\t\t\t// a monotonic clock that when subtracted do not represent the delta\n   254→\t\t\t// in wall clock time.\n   255→\t\t\tstart := time.Now().Round(0)\n   256→\t\t\tsch.metrics.BehindSeconds.Set(start.Sub(tick).Seconds())\n   257→\n   258→\t\t\tsch.processTick(ctx, dispatcherGroup, tick)\n   259→\n   260→\t\t\tsch.metrics.SchedulePeriodicDuration.Observe(time.Since(start).Seconds())\n   261→\t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n   262→\t\t\t// waiting for all rule evaluation routines to stop\n   263→\t\t\twaitErr := dispatcherGroup.Wait()\n   264→\t\t\treturn waitErr\n   265→\t\t}\n   266→\t}\n   267→}\n   268→\n   269→type readyToRunItem struct {\n   270→\truleRoutine Rule\n   271→\tEvaluation\n   272→}\n   273→\n   274→// TODO refactor to accept a callback for tests that will be called with things that are returned currently, and return nothing.\n   275→// Returns a slice of rules that were scheduled for evaluation, map of stopped rules, and a slice of updated rules\n   276→func (sch *schedule) processTick(ctx context.Context, dispatcherGroup *errgroup.Group, tick time.Time) ([]readyToRunItem, map[ngmodels.AlertRuleKey]struct{}, []ngmodels.AlertRuleKeyWithVersion) {\n   277→\ttickNum := tick.Unix() / int64(sch.baseInterval.Seconds())\n   278→\n   279→\t// update the local registry. If there was a difference between the previous state and the current new state, rulesDiff will contains keys of rules that were updated.\n   280→\trulesDiff, err := sch.updateSchedulableAlertRules(ctx)\n   281→\tupdated := rulesDiff.updated\n   282→\tif updated == nil { // make sure map is not nil\n   283→\t\tupdated = map[ngmodels.AlertRuleKey]struct{}{}\n   284→\t}\n   285→\tif err != nil {\n   286→\t\tsch.log.Error(\"Failed to update alert rules\", \"error\", err)\n   287→\t}\n   288→\n   289→\t// this is the new current state. rulesDiff contains the previously existing rules that were different between this state and the previous state.\n   290→\talertRules, folderTitles := sch.schedulableAlertRules.all()\n   291→\n   292→\t// registeredDefinitions is a map used for finding deleted alert rules\n   293→\t// initially it is assigned to all known alert rules from the previous cycle\n   294→\t// each alert rule found also in this cycle is removed\n   295→\t// so, at the end, the remaining registered alert rules are the deleted ones\n   296→\tregisteredDefinitions := sch.registry.keyMap()\n   297→\n   298→\tsch.updateRulesMetrics(alertRules)\n   299→\n   300→\treadyToRun := make([]readyToRunItem, 0)\n   301→\tupdatedRules := make([]ngmodels.AlertRuleKeyWithVersion, 0, len(updated)) // this is cancelled\")\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tif err != nil || results.HasErrors() {\n\t\tevalAttemptFailures.Inc()\n\n\t\t// Only retry (return errors) if this isn't the last attempt, otherwise skip these return operations.\n\t\tif retry {\n\t\t\t// The only thing that can return non-nil `err` from ruleEval.Evaluate is the server side expression pipeline.\n\t\t\t// This includes transport errors such !results.HasNonRetryableErrors() {\n\t\t\t\tspan.SetStatus(codes.Error, \"rule evaluation failed\")\n\t\t\t\tspan.RecordError(err)\n\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"the result-set has errors that can be nil\n}\n\n// send sends alerts for the given state transitions.\nfunc (a *alertRule) send(ctx context.Context, logger log.Logger, states state.StateTransitions) definitions.PostableAlerts {\n\talerts
